<td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" width="33"/> <i><a href="/wiki/2017_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_F.C._season" title="2017 São Paulo F.C. season">Current season</a></i></td>

</table>
<p><b>São Paulo Futebol Clube</b> (<small>Portuguese pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[sɐ̃w ˈpawlu fuʧiˈbɔw ˈklubi]</a></span>), simply known as <b>São Paulo</b>, is a professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club, based in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, Brazil.</p>
<p>The club plays in the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Paulista" title="Campeonato Paulista">Paulistão</a> (the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">State of São Paulo</a>'s premier <a href="/wiki/State_football_leagues_in_Brazil" title="State football leagues in Brazil">state league</a>), as well as the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Brasileirão</a> (the top tier of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_football_league_system" title="Brazilian football league system">Brazilian football league system</a>), being one of the only five clubs to have <a href="/wiki/List_of_unrelegated_association_football_clubs" title="List of unrelegated association football clubs">never been relegated</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas Flamengo">Flamengo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cruzeiro_Esporte_Clube" title="Cruzeiro Esporte Clube">Cruzeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Chapecoense_de_Futebol" title="Associação Chapecoense de Futebol">Chapecoense</a>.</p>
<p>As for international titles, São Paulo is the most successful team from Brazil, with 12 international titles. It is also one of the most successful South American clubs in terms of overall titles, having won 21 state titles, six <i>Brasileirão</i> titles, three <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> titles, one <a href="/wiki/Copa_Sudamericana" title="Copa Sudamericana">Copa Sudamericana</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Supercopa_Libertadores" title="Supercopa Libertadores">Supercopa Libertadores</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Copa_CONMEBOL" title="Copa CONMEBOL">Copa CONMEBOL</a>, one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copa_Masters_CONMEBOL" title="Copa Masters CONMEBOL">Copa Masters CONMEBOL</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Recopa_Sudamericana" title="Recopa Sudamericana">Recopa Sudamericanas</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cups</a> and one <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Founded in 1930, São Paulo was an inaugural member of the <i><a href="/wiki/Clube_dos_13" title="Clube dos 13">Clube dos 13</a></i> group of Brazil's leading football clubs. The club's most consistent spell of success came in the 1990s, under coach <a href="/wiki/Tel%C3%AA_Santana" title="Telê Santana">Telê Santana</a>, when it won three state titles, one national championship, two Copa Libertadores, two Recopa Sudamericanas, two Intercontinental Cups, one Supercopa Sudamericana, one Copa CONMEBOL, one Copa Masters CONMEBOL.</p>
<p>São Paulo is the third best-supported club in Brazil, with over 28 million supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-7">[7]</a></sup> The team's traditional home kit is a white shirt with two horizontal stripes (one red and one black), white shorts and white socks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-7">[7]</a></sup> Its home ground is the 67,052-seater <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Morumbi" title="Estádio do Morumbi">Morumbi</a> football stadium in São Paulo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> where it has played since 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morumbi_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-morumbi-9">[9]</a></sup> The stadium was the venue for the Copa Libertadores finals of 1992, 1993, 1994, 2000, 2003, 2005 and 2006. São Paulo is the second richest Brazilian football club in terms of revenue, with an annual revenue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Dollar" title="US Dollar">$111.9m</a> (<a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€78.2m</a>), and the second nation's most valuable club, worth over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Dollar" title="US Dollar">$353.4m</a> (<a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€246.9m</a>) in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1930.E2.80.931934:_Origins_of_the_club:_.22S.C3.A3o_Paulo_da_Floresta.22_.28.22S.C3.A3o_Paulo_of_the_Forest.22.29">1930–1934: Origins of the club: "São Paulo da Floresta" ("São Paulo of the Forest")</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title='Edit section: 1930–1934: Origins of the club: "São Paulo da Floresta" ("São Paulo of the Forest")'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1865" data-file-width="3387" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg/250px-Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg/375px-Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg/500px-Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Memorial_-_foundation_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The foundations of the club in 1930 and 1935 at the memorial Cássio Luiz dos Santos Werneck.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1205" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg/250px-SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg/375px-SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg/500px-SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SPFC_squad_-_1931_-_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The championship team of 1931</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>São Paulo FC was founded on 25 January 1930 by 60 former officials, players, members and friends of the football clubs <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CA_Paulistano" title="CA Paulistano">CA Paulistano</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=AA_das_Palmeiras&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="AA das Palmeiras (page does not exist)">AA das Palmeiras</a> of São Paulo. Paulistano, founded in 1900 and thus one of the oldest clubs in town and 11-time champions of São Paulo, abandoned football due to the professionalization of the sport. Palmeiras, founded in 1902 and three-time champions of São Paulo, intended after the end of the season 1929 to set up a professional team, but failed to do so.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Paulistano brought into the union star players like <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Friedenreich" title="Arthur Friedenreich">Arthur Friedenreich</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Araken_Patuska" title="Araken Patuska">Araken Patuska</a>. Palmeiras' contribution was the stadium <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Est%C3%A1dio_da_Floresta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Estádio da Floresta (page does not exist)">Estádio da Floresta</a>, generally known as <i>Chácara da Floresta</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The jerseys of the new club were derived from the ones of Palmeiras, which were white and sported a black ring across the chest. To the black-and-white of Palmeiras was added the red-and-white of Paulistano, thus, the ring became red, white and black.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The team, coached by former Paulistano star player <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rubens_Salles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rubens Salles (page does not exist)">Rubens Salles</a>, played its first match on 16 March 1930 when it drew 0–0 against <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=CA_Ypiranga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="CA Ypiranga (page does not exist)">CA Ypiranga</a>. The side became in the same year runner up of the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Paulista" title="Campeonato Paulista">State Championship</a> and won it in 1931, losing only one match of 26 and scoring 92 goals in the process. In the following three years São Paulo FC was again runner up in the championship.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1933, football in São Paulo became officially professional and the friendly match on March 12, 1933 which São Paulo won 5–1 against <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos FC</a> is considered the opener of that era.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Internal arguments and turmoil led to financial problems. The club merged with Clube de Regatas Tietê, another sports club from the town, and the football department was disbanded on 14 May 1935.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1935.E2.80.931939:_The_Rebirth_of_S.C3.A3o_Paulo_FC">1935–1939: The Rebirth of São Paulo FC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1935–1939: The Rebirth of São Paulo FC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Just after the merger with Tietê, the founders and re-founders created the Grêmio Tricolor, which formed Clube Atlético São Paulo on 4 June 1935, and, finally, São Paulo Futebol Clube on 16 December of the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-origins_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-origins-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new club's first game was against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Atl%C3%A9tica_Portuguesa_Santista" title="Associação Atlética Portuguesa Santista">Portuguesa Santista</a> on 25 January 1936. The match was almost cancelled, owing to the city's anniversary, but Porphyrio da Paz, the football director and composer of the club's anthem, obtained permission from the Board of Education Office for the game to continue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30s_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-30s-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another merger occurred in 1938, this time with Clube Atlético Estudantes Paulista, from the neighborhood of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mo%C3%B3ca" title="Moóca">Moóca</a>, and the club finished as runners-up in the Campeonato Paulista.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1940.E2.80.931950:_The_Steam_Roller">1940–1950: The Steam Roller</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1940–1950: The Steam Roller">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1940, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Pacaembu" title="Estádio do Pacaembu">Estádio do Pacaembu</a> was inaugurated, a new era began in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo state</a> football. São Paulo Futebol Clube finished as runners-up once again in the Campeonato Paulista in 1941, and a year later the club paid 200 <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">contos de réis</a> (equivalent to approximately R$162,000 today) to acquire <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B4nidas" title="Leônidas">Leônidas</a> from <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a>. During this period, São Paulo also acquired the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentinian_people" title="Argentinian people">Argentinian</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Sastre" title="Antonio Sastre">António Sastre</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" title="Brazilian people">Brazilians</a> <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Eduardo_Barreto_de_Freitas_Noronha" title="Alfredo Eduardo Barreto de Freitas Noronha">Noronha</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Bauer" title="José Carlos Bauer">José Carlos Bauer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zez%C3%A9_Proc%C3%B3pio" title="Zezé Procópio">Zezé Procópio</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADz_Mesquita_de_Oliveira" title="Luíz Mesquita de Oliveira">Luizinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rui_Campos" title="Rui Campos">Rui</a> and Teixeirinha. With these new additions, <i>Tricolor</i> became known as the <i>Steam Roller</i>, winning the Paulista championship five times, in 1943, 1945, 1946, 1948 and 1949. The club sold its <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Canind%C3%A9" title="Estádio do Canindé">Canindé</a> training ground to <a href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Portuguesa_de_Desportos" title="Associação Portuguesa de Desportos">Portuguesa</a> to raise money for their new stadium the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Morumbi" title="Estádio do Morumbi">Estádio do Morumbi</a>, for which construction began in 1952.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="1024" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg/250px-SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg/375px-SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg/500px-SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SPFC_squad_-_1936_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New team after being reformed in 1936</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1951.E2.80.931957:_The_Dry_Spell">1951–1957: The Dry Spell</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1951–1957: The Dry Spell">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The run of success of the 1940s, came to an end in the early 1950s, and the club only won two state championships in the new decade, in 1953 and 1957. The latter championship was won with the help of the 35-year-old Brazilian international <a href="/wiki/Zizinho" title="Zizinho">Zizinho</a> and Hungarian manager <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Guttmann" title="Béla Guttmann">Béla Guttmann</a>. In the years that followed, the club struggled to compete with the rise of <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> and his club, Santos. With the construction of the Morumbi stadium still ongoing, São Paulo entered its longest period without a title in its history, which was to last 13 years.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Le%C3%B4nidas_da_Silva_and_Arthur_Friedenreich_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="256" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Le%C3%B4nidas_da_Silva_and_Arthur_Friedenreich_01.jpg/220px-Le%C3%B4nidas_da_Silva_and_Arthur_Friedenreich_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Le%C3%B4nidas_da_Silva_and_Arthur_Friedenreich_01.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Le%C3%B4nidas_da_Silva_and_Arthur_Friedenreich_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B4nidas" title="Leônidas">Leônidas</a> with another <i>Tricolor</i> legend, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Friedenreich" title="Arthur Friedenreich">Arthur Friedenreich</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1958.E2.80.931969:_Just_the_Stadium">1958–1969: Just the Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1958–1969: Just the Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since São Paulo's budget planning was focused on the Estádio do Morumbi construction rather than the signing of new players, few expensive players were bought during the 1960s, although the club did acquire Brazilian internationals <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Dias" title="Roberto Dias">Roberto Dias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jurandir_de_Freitas" title="Jurandir de Freitas">Jurandir</a>. In 1960, the Estádio do Morumbi was inaugurated, named after the late Cícero Pompeu de Toledo, the club's chairman during most of the stadium construction. One of the few happy moments for the fans during this period was the 1963 Paulista Championship 4–1 victory against Pelé's Santos.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.931979:_Campeonato_Brasileiro_.28Brazilian_Championship.29">1970–1979: Campeonato Brasileiro (Brazilian Championship)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1970–1979: Campeonato Brasileiro (Brazilian Championship)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1970, the Estádio do Morumbi was finally completed and the club purchased <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rson" title="Gérson">Gérson</a> from <a href="/wiki/Botafogo_de_Futebol_e_Regatas" title="Botafogo de Futebol e Regatas">Botafogo</a>, Uruguayan midfielder <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Rocha" title="Pedro Rocha">Pedro Rocha</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1arol" title="Peñarol">Peñarol</a> and striker <a href="/wiki/Toninho_Guerreiro" title="Toninho Guerreiro">Toninho Guerreiro</a> from Santos. The club was managed by <a href="/wiki/Zez%C3%A9_Moreira" title="Zezé Moreira">Zezé Moreira</a>, who was the manager of <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> at the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1954 FIFA World Cup">1954</a>, and won the Paulista Championship after beating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarani_Futebol_Clube" title="Guarani Futebol Clube">Guarani</a> 2–1 in the <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a> a week before the end of the competition.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2360" data-file-width="8165" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg/450px-Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg/675px-Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg/900px-Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg 2x" width="450"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_panoramic_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Morumbi" title="Estádio do Morumbi">Morumbi Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1971, the club beat <a href="/wiki/Sociedade_Esportiva_Palmeiras" title="Sociedade Esportiva Palmeiras">Palmeiras</a> 1–0 with a goal from <a href="/wiki/Toninho_Guerreiro" title="Toninho Guerreiro">Toninho Guerreiro</a> in the final to capture another state title. That year saw the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro</a>, with the club finishing as runners-up to <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro" title="Clube Atlético Mineiro">Atlético Mineiro</a>, managed by <a href="/wiki/Tel%C3%AA_Santana" title="Telê Santana">Telê Santana</a>.</p>
<p>In the following years, São Paulo and Palmeiras gradually overtook Pelé's Santos and <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Corinthians</a> as the dominant club sides in São Paulo state. In 1972, Palmeiras won the state championship title, only one point ahead of São Paulo, and the following year the clubs finished in the same positions in the <a href="/wiki/1973_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1973 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Brazilian Championship</a>. In 1974, São Paulo took part in the <a href="/wiki/1974_Copa_Libertadores" title="1974 Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> losing in the final to <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Independiente" title="Club Atlético Independiente">Independiente</a> in a replay.</p>
<p>In 1975, former goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Poy" title="José Poy">José Poy</a> took over as manager, and São Paulo won the Paulista Championship after defeating <a href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Portuguesa_de_Desportos" title="Associação Portuguesa de Desportos">Portuguesa</a> in a penalty shoot-out.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valdir_Peres" title="Valdir Peres">Valdir Peres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chic%C3%A3o" title="Chicão">Chicão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serginho_Chulapa" title="Serginho Chulapa">Serginho Chulapa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%A9_S%C3%A9rgio" title="Zé Sérgio">Zé Sérgio</a> were the club's most influential players when São Paulo finally secured the Brazilian Championship for the first time in <a href="/wiki/1977_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1977 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1977</a> following a penalty shoot-out victory over Atlético Mineiro at the <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a>. However, they failed to win another trophy until the reclaimed the Paulista Championship in 1980.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_1980s:_Tricolor_Decade">The 1980s: Tricolor Decade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The 1980s: Tricolor Decade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1980s, São Paulo won four Paulista and one Brazilian titles, helped by the impressive central defensive pair of <a href="/wiki/Oscar_(footballer,_born_1954)" title="Oscar (footballer, born 1954)">Oscar</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dario_Pereyra" title="Dario Pereyra">Dario Pereyra</a>. 1980 and 1981, the club won the Paulista Championship in successive seasons for the first time since the 1940s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80s_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-80s-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1985, the head coach <a href="/wiki/Cilinho" title="Cilinho">Cilinho</a> introduced to the world the <i><a href="/wiki/Menudo_(band)" title="Menudo (band)">Menudos</a> of Morumbi</i>, a team that included <a href="/wiki/Silas_Pereira" title="Silas Pereira">Paulo Silas</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCller_(footballer)" title="Müller (footballer)">Müller</a> and Sidney, and the club once again won the Paulista Championship. The main striker was <a href="/wiki/Careca" title="Careca">Careca</a>, a centre-forward who also played for <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 FIFA World Cup</a>. The midfield featured <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Roberto_Falc%C3%A3o" title="Paulo Roberto Falcão">Falcão</a>, brought in from Italian club <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>, where he earned the nicknamed <i>King of Rome</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80s_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-80s-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1986_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1986 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1986</a>, manager <a href="/wiki/Pepe_(footballer,_born_1935)" title="Pepe (footballer, born 1935)">Pepe</a> led the club to its second Brazilian Championship title, defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarani_Futebol_Clube" title="Guarani Futebol Clube">Guarani</a> in a penalty shoot-out. In 1987, Dario Pereyra left the club, but in that year the <i>Menudos</i> team won its last title, another Paulista title. The so-called <i>Tricolor Decade</i> ended with the 1989 Paulista Championship title and a second-place finish in the Brazilian Championship, when São Paulo lost to <a href="/wiki/CR_Vasco_da_Gama" title="CR Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> in the final match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80s_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-80s-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990.E2.80.931995:_The_Tel.C3.AA_Era.5B15.5D">1990–1995: The Telê Era<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tele_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tele-15">[15]</a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1990–1995: The Telê Era[15]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1055" data-file-width="1055" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg/220px-Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg/330px-Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg/440px-Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tel%C3%AA_Santana_da_Silva_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tel%C3%AA_Santana" title="Telê Santana">Telê Santana</a>, won two Copa Libertadores and two Club World Cups with São Paulo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1990, after a poor start to the campaign in Championship Paulista, Telê Santana was hired as the club's coach, and São Paulo went on to finish runners-up in the Brazilian Championship. In 1991, Santana won his first title after winning the Paulista championship.</p>
<p>In 1991, São Paulo won the Brazilian championship after beating <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Alberto_Parreira" title="Carlos Alberto Parreira">Carlos Alberto Parreira</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Bragantino" title="Clube Atlético Bragantino">Bragantino</a>, and the club began a period of consistent achievement both nationally and internationally. The following year they reached the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> final, where they faced <a href="/wiki/Newell%27s_Old_Boys" title="Newell's Old Boys">Newell's Old Boys</a> of Argentina. São Paulo lost the first leg 1–0, but reversed the scoreline in the second leg in Brazil, and then won the competition in the penalty shoot-out to take the title for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="538" data-file-width="538" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg/220px-Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg/330px-Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg/440px-Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ra%C3%AD_Souza_Vieira_de_Oliveira_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AD" title="Raí">Raí</a>, São Paulo's midfielder in the 1990s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the same year, in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> the club won its first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European/South_American_Cup" title="European/South American Cup">Intercontinental Cup</a>, beating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johann_Cruyff" title="Johann Cruyff">Johann Cruyff</a>'s <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> 2–1. After returning to Brazil, the club beat Palmeiras 2–1 to win its 18th state championship title.</p>
<p>In 1993, São Paulo retained the Copa Libertadores, beating <a href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Universidad_Cat%C3%B3lica" title="Club Deportivo Universidad Católica">Universidad Católica</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> in the final. After the competition, influential midfielder <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AD" title="Raí">Raí</a> left the club, but São Paulo won the Intercontinental Cup again, beating <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Capello" title="Fabio Capello">Fabio Capello</a>'s <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> 3–2. Müller scored the winning goal in the 86th minute of the match, from an assist by <a href="/wiki/Toninho_Cerezo" title="Toninho Cerezo">Toninho Cerezo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Title_93_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Title_93-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1994, the club reached the final of the Copa Libertadores for the third year in a row, and faced Argentina's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_V%C3%A9lez_S%C3%A1rsfield" title="Club Atlético Vélez Sársfield">Vélez Sársfield</a>. On this occasion they lost a penalty shoot-out to the Argentine side at the Morumbi stadium. But by the end of this year, São Paulo won the <a href="/wiki/Copa_CONMEBOL" title="Copa CONMEBOL">Copa CONMEBOL</a>, defeating Peñarol of Uruguay in the final.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996.E2.80.932004:_Post-Tel.C3.AA_years">1996–2004: Post-Telê years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1996–2004: Post-Telê years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rogerio_ceni.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1572" data-file-width="904" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Rogerio_ceni.jpg/175px-Rogerio_ceni.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Rogerio_ceni.jpg/263px-Rogerio_ceni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Rogerio_ceni.jpg/350px-Rogerio_ceni.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rogerio_ceni.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rogério Ceni, São Paulo's former goalkeeper, he is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_goalscoring_goalkeepers" title="List of goalscoring goalkeepers">highest scoring goalkeeper of all time.</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the beginning of 1996, owing to health issues, Telê Santana left São Paulo, ending the club's golden era. Between 1995 and 2004, the club had fourteen managers. Among the most notable titles during those ten years were the 2000 Paulista Championship and the club's first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torneio_Rio-S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Torneio Rio-São Paulo">Rio-São Paulo Tournament</a> title in 2001. <a href="/wiki/Rog%C3%A9rio_Ceni" title="Rogério Ceni">Rogério Ceni</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_Baptista" title="Júlio Baptista">Júlio Baptista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Fabiano" title="Luís Fabiano">Luís Fabiano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kak%C3%A1" title="Kaká">Kaká</a> were the club's stars. Raí briefly returned to the club between 1998 and 2000, and with him, the club won the Paulista Championship twice, in 1998 and 2000, after beating Corinthians and Santos, respectively. In 2004 São Paulo were back in the Copa Libertadores and reached the semi-finals before being eliminated by underdogs <a href="/wiki/Once_Caldas" title="Once Caldas">Once Caldas</a> from Colombia. At the end of that year, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89merson_Le%C3%A3o" title="Émerson Leão">Émerson Leão</a> was hired as the club's coach.</p>
<p>In 2003, São Paulo made a deal with Spanish amateur side Santangelo Club Aficionado that resulted in the Spanish club changing its name to <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Madrid" title="São Paulo Madrid">São Paulo Madrid</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.93present">2005–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2005–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2005, with Leão as the club's manager, São Paulo won the Paulista Championship. Leão, however, would soon leave the club with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paulo_Autuori_de_Mello" title="Paulo Autuori de Mello">Paulo Autuori</a>, former manager of the <a href="/wiki/Peru_national_football_team" title="Peru national football team">Peru national team</a>, hired to replace him. São Paulo won the Libertadores Cup for the third time, beating another Brazilian side, <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Paranaense" title="Clube Atlético Paranaense">Atlético Paranaense</a>, in the final. Atlético switched the first leg of the final to <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Beira-Rio" title="Estádio Beira-Rio">Estádio Beira-Rio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, their own ground not having sufficient capacity for a final, and the match ended in a 1–1 draw. In the second leg, at the Morumbi, São Paulo won 4–0 to become the first Brazilian club to win three Copa Libertadores titles.</p>
<p>In December 2005, São Paulo competed in the <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2005 FIFA Club World Championship">FIFA Club World Championship</a> in Japan. After beating <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Ittihad_(Jeddah)" title="Al-Ittihad (Jeddah)">Al-Ittihad</a> 3–2, they faced European champions <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in the final. A 1–0 victory over the English team gave São Paulo its third intercontinental title. The single goal was scored by <a href="/wiki/Mineiro_(footballer)" title="Mineiro (footballer)">Mineiro</a> in the first half of the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Other players in that year's squad included centre-back <a href="/wiki/Diego_Lugano" title="Diego Lugano">Diego Lugano</a>, full-back <a href="/wiki/Cicinho" title="Cicinho">Cicinho</a> and forward <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rcio_Amoroso" title="Márcio Amoroso">Amoroso</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1252" data-file-width="2480" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg/300px-SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg/450px-SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg/600px-SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SPFC_squad_-_2005_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tribute received from the Paulista Football Federation and President Lula for winning the first FIFA Club World Cup.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the success of the 2005 season, Paulo Autuori left the team to coach <a href="/wiki/Kashima_Antlers" title="Kashima Antlers">Kashima Antlers</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._League_Division_1" title="J. League Division 1">J. League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Muricy_Ramalho" title="Muricy Ramalho">Muricy Ramalho</a> was signed up as the new coach, having led <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Internacional" title="Sport Club Internacional">Internacional</a> to the runners-up position in the 2005 Brazilian Championship. In his first tournament as a manager, Ramalho reached second place in the Paulista Championship, losing to Santos by one point. São Paulo reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Copa_Libertadores" title="2006 Copa Libertadores">2006 Copa Libertadores</a>, but lost 4–3 on aggregate to Brazilian rivals <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Internacional" title="Sport Club Internacional">Internacional</a>. However, they went on to win their fourth <a href="/wiki/2006_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2006 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro</a> trophy, becoming the first team to become national champions in the new <a href="/wiki/League_system" title="League system">league system</a> format.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="1024" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg/200px-Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg/300px-Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg/400px-Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bayern_vs_Sao_Paulo_at_Hong_Kong.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
São Paulo against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich" title="Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> in 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After being eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/2007_Copa_Libertadores" title="2007 Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> in 2007, São Paulo won the Brazilian title for the second year in a row, fifteen points ahead of second-placed <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos</a>. They won the title for the third season running in 2008 season, overturning an 11-point deficit behind <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%AAmio_Foot-Ball_Porto_Alegrense" title="Grêmio Foot-Ball Porto Alegrense">Grêmio</a>, to become the first team win the national title six times. Manager Muricy Ramalho was also the first manager to win three Brazilian titles in a row with the same team.</p>
<p>Ramalho was fired from the manager post following a defeat in the home leg of the <a href="/wiki/2009_Copa_Libertadores" title="2009 Copa Libertadores">2009 Copa Libertadores</a> to Cruzeiro, São Paulo's fourth consecutive Libertadores Cup elimination to another Brazilian. <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Gomes" title="Ricardo Gomes">Ricardo Gomes</a> took over as manager.</p>
<p>In 2010 São Paulo lost again against <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Internacional" title="Sport Club Internacional">Internacional</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Copa_Libertadores" title="2010 Copa Libertadores">2010 Libertadores Cup</a>, ending Ricardo Gomes's spell as manager. In 2011, the club signed <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a> and purchased Luís Fabiano for a club-record €7.6 million from <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a>. Goalkeeper Rogério Ceni, meanwhile, scored his 100th career goal, against Corinthians.</p>
<p>In research conducted by Brazilian sports website GloboEsporte.com, São Paulo, during the eight years between 2003 and 2011, were just the second Brazilian club to earn more money than losses in the transfer market – <i>Tricolor paulista</i> received <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">R$</a>287 million, behind only Internacional, which earned R$289 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the 2013 season, after seven years wearing kits produced by <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>, São Paulo signed with Brazilian brand <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_(Brazilian_sports_manufacturer)" title="Penalty (Brazilian sports manufacturer)">Penalty</a>. The contract was valid until 2015 and the club earned R$35 million per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> This contract was the second-most lucrative kit deal in Brazil, just exceeded by Flamengo and <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>' deal of R$38 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In May 2015, São Paulo presented its new kits, made by <a href="/wiki/Under_Armour" title="Under Armour">Under Armour</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours_and_badge">Colours and badge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Colours and badge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When <b>Club Athletico Paulistano</b> and <b>Associação Atlética das Palmeiras</b> merged, their colours (red and white for Paulistano and black and white for Palmeiras) were inherited by São Paulo. The colours match those of São Paulo's state flag, and also represent the three main races that lived in Brazil during that period: the Native Americans (represented by the red), the Europeans (represented by the white) and the Africans (represented by the black).</p>
<p>The club's home strip is a white shirt, with two horizontal stripes at chest level, the upper one red and the lower one black, and with a badge in the centre of the chest. The shorts and socks are all-white. The away strip consists of a red shirt with red, black and white vertical stripes, black shorts and socks.</p>
<p>The badge consists of a shield with a black rectangle in the upper section bearing the initials SPFC in white. Below the rectangle is a red, white and black triangle. The badge also has five stars, two gold and three red ones. The gold ones denote <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adhemar_Ferreira_da_Silva" title="Adhemar Ferreira da Silva">Adhemar Ferreira da Silva</a>'s world and Olympic records and the red ones represents the three world championships won by São Paulo.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg/250px-Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg/375px-Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg/500px-Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cicero_pompeu_de_toledo_-_inside_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Estádio do Morumbi (Morumbi Stadium), inside view</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Morumbi" title="Estádio do Morumbi">Estádio do Morumbi</a></div>
<p>São Paulo's stadium is officially named <i>Estádio Cícero Pompeu de Toledo</i> (Cicero Pompeu de Toledo Stadium) and commonly known by the nickname <i>Estádio do Morumbi</i> (Morumbi Stadium). It was inaugurated in 1960, with a maximum sitting capacity of 120,000 people, but now its maximum capacity is only 67,052 seats. Its record attendance for a football match, set in 1977, is 146,082.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morumbi_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-morumbi-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club also owns two training grounds, one named <i>Centro de Treinamento Frederico Antônio Germano Menzen</i> (Frederico Antônio Germano Menzen Training Center), nicknamed <i>Centro de Treinamento (CT) da Barra Funda</i> (Barra Funda's Training Center), which is used mostly by the professional team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctbarrafunda_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-ctbarrafunda-25">[25]</a></sup> The other is the <i>Centro de Formação de Atletas Presidente Laudo Natel</i> (President Laudo Natel Athletes Formation Center), nicknamed <i>Centro de Treinamento (CT) de Cotia</i> (Cotia's Training Center), which is used by the youth teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cotia_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cotia-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_rivalries">Club rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Club rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S.C3.A3o_Paulo_vs._Palmeiras"><i>São Paulo vs. Palmeiras</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: São Paulo vs. Palmeiras">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Choque-Rei" title="Choque-Rei">Choque-Rei</a></div>
<p>This fixture is nicknamed the "Choque Rei", and has seen 103 wins by São Paulo, 99 wins by Palmeiras and 99 draws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S.C3.A3o_Paulo_vs._Santos"><i>São Paulo vs. Santos</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: São Paulo vs. Santos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/San-S%C3%A3o" title="San-São">San-São</a></div>
<p>Also known as "San-São", this fixture was first played in 1936. Since then, São Paulo have won it 114 times, Santos 92, and there have been 62 draws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S.C3.A3o_Paulo_vs._Corinthians"><i>São Paulo vs. Corinthians</i></span><i><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: São Paulo vs. Corinthians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1ssico_Majestoso" title="Clássico Majestoso">Clássico Majestoso</a></div>
<p>The game between these clubs is also known as "Majestoso", a name coined by Thomas Mazzoni. The first "Majestoso" occurred on 25 May 1930.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The fixture has seen 79 wins for São Paulo, 88 wins for Corinthians and 84 draws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
